       <article class="post-27382 post type-post status-publish format-standard hentry category-contests tag-demons tag-vampires post-listing">
        <div class="single-post-thumb">
        </div>
        <div class="post-inner">
         <h1 class="name post-title entry-title" itemprop="itemReviewed" itemscope="" itemtype="http://schema.org/Thing">
          <span itemprop="name">
           Author Sharon Ashwood Release Party and Contest
          </span>
         </h1>
         <p class="post-meta">
          <span class="post-meta-author">
           Posted by:
           <a href="http://bittenbybooks.com/author/site-hostess/" title="">
            Site Hostess
           </a>
          </span>
          <span class="post-cats">
           in
           <a href="http://bittenbybooks.com/category/contests-and-giveaways/contests/" rel="category tag" title="View all posts in Contests">
            Contests
           </a>
          </span>
          <span class="tie-date">
           July 8, 2010
          </span>
          <span class="post-comments">
           <a href="http://bittenbybooks.com/author-sharon-ashwood-release-party-and-contest-live-here/#comments" title="Comment on Author Sharon Ashwood Release Party and Contest">
            239 Comments
           </a>
          </span>
          <span class="post-views">
           767 Views
          </span>
         </p>
         <div class="clear">
         </div>
         <div class="entry">
          <p>
           <a href="http://www.amazon.com/gp/product/0451230736?ie=UTF8&amp;tag=bittenbybooks-20&amp;linkCode=as2&amp;camp=1789&amp;creative=390957&amp;creativeASIN=0451230736">
            <img alt="" class="alignleft size-full wp-image-27307" height="160" src="../wp-content/uploads/2010/07/unchained1.jpg" title="Click this image now to buy your copy of Unchained by Sharon Ashwood" width="99"/>
           </a>
          </p>
          <p>
           <strong>
            PLEASE NOTE: The contest portion of the Sharon Ashwood event is now closed. The winners will be chosen at a later date and notified via email.
           </strong>
          </p>
          <p>
           Been there, slain that.
          </p>
          <p>
           Ashe Carver wants out of the monster-removal biz.  She has to prove shes a good mother if she wants to retain custody of her ten-year-old-daughterso she takes a low-paying job at the library and tries to live on the straight and narrow.
           <br/>
           <span id="more-27382">
           </span>
           <br/>
           How characters evolve is a fascinating process. Every imaginary world thats packed with monsters has a hunter archetype, all the way back to Draculas Vanhelsing. When I first created Ashe, she was an uncomplicated, butt-kicking killer of monsters.  Then I started to wonder how a slayer would really fare in my story world, where not all the non-humans are bad guys. Rumbling around on a motorcycle staking vampires sounds cool, but when a girl has to be choosy about who she kills, things can get stressful.
          </p>
          <p>
           And then it turned out that Ashe had a ten-year-old daughter. That opened up a whole other side to her personality. Suddenly, rather than just a leather-clad Slayer Barbie, my character was a single mom, a widow, a sister, an employee, a witch, a huntershe was like every other adult woman I know, wearing a dozen hats and trying desperately to balance everyones needs.
          </p>
          <p>
           Of course, there is a crisis. After centuries guarding a supernatural prison, Captain Reynard is suddenly free to join the modern worldbut only to solve a crime. Brave, honourable, and devastatingly handsome, he has mere weeks to live unless Ashe finds the thief who took his soul.
          </p>
          <p>
           Ashe picks up her weapons again, risking everything to help him. Everything goes deeper than just her physical safety. Everything means reliving every last nightmare of her tragic lifeand sacrificing an unexpected gift of love.
          </p>
          <p>
           The bigger the stakespun intendedthe bigger the reward. Ashe and Reynard put it all on the line, but its the only way to break the chains that bind them.
          </p>
          <p>
           But my books are never entirely serious. Just to prove the point, check out Ashes do-it-yourself monster removal advice for those who might be suffering from a supernatural infestation around the home or office.
           <a href="http://www.sharonashwood.com/diy-advice.php" target="_blank" title="check it out here">
            http://www.sharonashwood.com/diy-advice.php
           </a>
           Whether youre dealing with goblins, changelings, imps, werewolves, fire demons . . . virtually any supernatural creature, Ashe has the advice you need to kick some serious monster butt!
          </p>
          <p>
           Who is your favourite slayer character?
          </p>
          <p>
           Who is your all-time favourite vampire?
          </p>
          <p>
           Do you prefer characters who have strong family ties, or the lone wolf types?
           <br/>
           .** .** .** .** .** .*
           <br/>
           <object classid="clsid:d27cdb6e-ae6d-11cf-96b8-444553540000" codebase="http://download.macromedia.com/pub/shockwave/cabs/flash/swflash.cab#version=6,0,40,0" height="322" width="394">
            <param name="allowFullScreen" value="true">
            </param>
            <param name="allowscriptaccess" value="always">
            </param>
            <param name="src" value="http://www.youtube.com/v/wbExjMvR8-0&amp;hl=en_US&amp;fs=1?rel=0&amp;color1=0x5d1719&amp;color2=0xcd311b&amp;border=1">
            </param>
            <embed allowfullscreen="true" allowscriptaccess="always" height="322" src="http://www.youtube.com/v/wbExjMvR8-0&amp;hl=en_US&amp;fs=1?rel=0&amp;color1=0x5d1719&amp;color2=0xcd311b&amp;border=1" type="application/x-shockwave-flash" width="394">
            </embed>
           </object>

          <p>
           <strong>
            <strong>
             1. Please note, the prize stated IS the prize you will  receive, there will be absolutely no substitutions or changes the prize is  non-transferable. If you dont want the prize being offered, please dont enter  the contest. If you ever win an electronic copy of a book, please note that it  is ILLEGAL to forward, give away or copy it in anyway once you receive it. Doing  so violates copyright. If we find out that it has been done, you will no longer  be eligible to win any of our contests.
             <br/>
             2. You have FIVE days from the day  the we contact you to claim your prize by sending your name/mailing address to  me. Failure to contact me will forfeit your prize. BBB can at that time, choose  either to re-award the prize to another entrant or not.
             <br/>
             3. The prize stated  IS the prize you will receive, there will be no substitutions, trades or  changes. No exceptions. Please do not ask. If for some reason you do not wish to  claim your prize, please let me know as soon as possible. Bitten by Books has  the option to re-award it or not.
             <br/>
             4. Contest is open to readers in the USA  except where noted above. The prizes are shipped directly from the publisher  unless otherwise noted.
             <br/>
             5. Bitten by Books is in NO way responsible for the  prizes being offered in any of the contests. If for some reason a contributor  does not honor their prize, there is nothing we can or will do about it. We are  not worried that this will happen, but we want to be very clear that WE are not  offering these prizes, the contributor is and it is their responsibility to  fulfill their prize obligations.
             <br/>
             6. These rules are subject to change or be  modified without prior written notice.
             <br/>
             7. Contest is void where  prohibited.
             <br/>
             8. By entering this contest you are agreeing to our terms of  entry
            </strong>
           </strong>
          </p>

             <div class="comment-content">
              <p>
               Hi, Viki!
              </p>
              <p>
               I think most women have to juggle a lot these days. I dont have children myself, but when you add job, writing, parents, friends, and until recently school together, it makes for a very busy life. People seem to be far busier than they used to be, and theres no reason my characters would get a pass just because they live in a world where the supernatural is present.  To my mind, that just makes their wide array of responsibilities that much more urgent.
              </p>
              <p>
               Besides, who says you cant be a mother and still kick monster butt?
              </p>
             </div>

            <p>
             I cant say that I have a favorite slayer or vampire. I like so many of them that I have read. There are always different things that draw me to each one, so its hard to pick a fave.
            </p>
            <p>
             As far as family tiesI think its interesting to find a charcter who has the ties, but may not actually know it. Its neat to watch them come to terms of being a lone wolf to having someone there for them.
            </p>
            <p>
             It looks like there is a fair amount of humor in this book. Did you plan it that way or did it just hapen as you wrote?
            </p>
            <p>
             I RSVPed, too.
            </p>
            <p>
             Thanks!
            </p>
            <p>
             Lanae T.
            </p>
           </div>
           <div class="reply">
           </div>

                July 8, 2010 at 1:53 pm
               </a>
              </div>
              <!-- .comment-meta .commentmetadata -->
             </div>
             <div class="clear">
             </div>
             <div class="comment-content">
              <p>
               Hi, Lanae,
              </p>
              <p>
               I think the paranormal goes down better with a twist of humour.  Also, most of life is pretty ridiculous to my twisted way of thinking, so a lot of it just comes out naturally. Also the characters viewpoint influences how they see the world.  Mac in SCORCHED was a natural comedian and that really came through.  He got some of my best lines ever. Reynard in UNCHAINED has a very dry sense of humour. Hes very serious at first glance, but beneath that is someone who can look at the most terrible situation and find courage. He stays strong in part because he hasnt forgotten how to laugh. That refusal to despair takes a lot of moral strength.
              </p>
             </div>
             <div class="reply">
             </div>

              <div class="comment-meta commentmetadata">
               <a href="http://bittenbybooks.com/author-sharon-ashwood-release-party-and-contest-live-here/#comment-167558">
                July 8, 2010 at 7:19 pm
               </a>
              </div>
              <!-- .comment-meta .commentmetadata -->
             </div>
             <div class="clear">
             </div>
             <div class="comment-content">
              <p>
               Hi, Seraphina,
              </p>
              <p>
               Your favorites are some of my favorites, too!  I didnt start out with an overall story arc, but I did by about the middle of SCORCHED. Im really interested in the way the series is going, and thats such an enormous boon to an author.  If youre not engaged, sitting down to write thousands and thousands of words is pure tortureand usually you give up. Thats not the case at all with me; Im excited and anxious to keep going!
              </p>
              <p>
               I worked on RAVENOUS for a couple of years.  I wasnt under contract for it and had all the time in the world to fiddle around.  It went through some pretty significant changes before it became what it is now  it started out in first person and with a different hero.  Im glad it turned out the way it did.
              </p>
             </div>
             <div class="reply">

              <p>
               Hi, Kisah,
              </p>
              <p>
               I fall between the plotter and the wanderer in the mistI need some structure or I go off the rails, but if I pin things down too much there arent any surprises for me.
              </p>
              <p>
               I read all kinds of genres, although more PNR romance and UF than anything else. Id love to write mysteries. I really admire an author who can keep me guessing right until the end, and then the answer is so logical I want to slap myself for not figuring it out!
              </p>

             </div>
             <div class="clear">
             </div>
             <div class="comment-content">
              <p>
               Hi, Mary,
              </p>
              <p>
               I cant imagine NOT writing some real life problems into a character, because thats where I connect with them. If a vampire has problems getting his dark wash clean without it fading, we have something in common. Also, the more concrete I can make my story world to the reader, the more they will accept the magical parts.  I actually think I first heard that writing tip from Laurell K. Hamilton!
              </p>
             </div>
             <div class="reply">

I dont really know the cause, but whatever works is okay by me.  My father died of stomach cancer, so Im not about to push my luck.

            </p>
            <p>
             2. My favorite all time vampire. That is just way too hard to narrow down. I love Spike. I mean how can you not. Lets see, Stefan from Patricia Briggs. Pretty much any of the Black Dagger Brotherhood. Please dont make me choose! I could keep going, but then Id be here all day.
            </p>
            <p>
             3. Lone Wolf or strong family ties. Both have their appeal. I can go for either, and I definitely have enough books in by TBR pile to support that! But Im always interested in the ones with someone else besides a significant other like a child. I like to see what kind of dynamic will evolve in a story with a kid involved.
            </p>
            <p>
             I have to ask about the picture of the cat in the sink on your website. I myself have found my cats in some pretty weird places. So what is the story behind that picture? Do you have any other animals?

              <!-- .comment-meta .commentmetadata -->
             </div>
             <div class="clear">
             </div>
             <div class="comment-content">
              <p>
               Hi, Patrick!
              </p>
              <p>
               My inspiration comes from everywhere.  A lot comes from the news, from courses Ive taken about economics and law, from folk and fairy tale, and from people watching. A writer is a bit like a blender. Lots goes in, gets swirled around, and comes out in new combinations.
              </p>
              <p>
               In answer to your sons great question  I havent done a character based just on one person, but sometimes bits of people I know find their way into my people.
              </p>
             </div>
             <div class="reply">

            </p>
            <p>
             I RSVPd.
             <br/>
             Fav. vampire  Eric from True Blood (Sookie Stackhouse)
            </p>
            <p>
             My question:
             <br/>
             What do you think of the fact that vampires are so trendy right now?
            </p>

         <li id="comment-167473">

           <div class="comment-avatar">
            <img alt="" class="avatar avatar-45 photo" height="45" src="http://1.gravatar.com/avatar/dc54259ec8f928b48431c2ea5f079e1a?s=45&amp;d=http%3A%2F%2Fbittenbybooks.com%2Fwp-content%2Fplugins%2Frage-avatars%2Favatars%2F016-everything-went-better-than-expected.png&amp;r=X" width="45"/>
           </div>
           <div class="author-comment">
            <cite class="fn">
             Barbara Elness
            </cite>
            <div class="comment-meta commentmetadata">
             <a href="http://bittenbybooks.com/author-sharon-ashwood-release-party-and-contest-live-here/#comment-167473">
              July 8, 2010 at 3:33 pm
             </a>
            </div>
            <!-- .comment-meta .commentmetadata -->
           </div>
           <div class="clear">
           </div>
           <div class="comment-content">
            <p>
             Its hard to answer your questions because there are so many great choices.  My favorite slayer character would be Keri Arthurs Riley Jenson, shes just doesnt stop until shes finished the job, no matter what it takes.  My all-time favorite vampire is Jeaniene Frosts Bones, hes just so bad-ass, but tender to his lady.
             <br/>
             I prefer characters that have strong ties, not necessarily to family, but to their friends or their made family.  It gives them more to lose, and more to fight for.
            </p>
            <p>
             I havent had a chance to read this series yet, but the books are definitely on my to buy list.
            </p>
            <p>
             RSVPd, attended &amp; commented on Erin Kellison
            </p>

           <div class="clear">
           </div>
           <div class="comment-content">
            <p>
             Hi, Sharon,
            </p>
            <p>
             Im new to reading your writing, but I love the sounds of AsheI like those layered characters, who are kind of like a lot of us, who juggle all kinds of responsibilities
             <img alt=":)" class="wp-smiley" src="http://bittenbybooks.com/wp-includes/images/smilies/icon_smile.gif"/>
            </p>
            <p>
             As for a favorite slayer, I guess for now, its still Buffyshe seems the iconic, kick-ass heroine who launched so much of this paranormal stuff into the mainstream
            </p>
            <p>
             My all-time favorite vampire is probably Count von CountIve loved his accent since *I* was a kid, plus hes educational
             <img alt=";)" class="wp-smiley" src="http://bittenbybooks.com/wp-includes/images/smilies/icon_wink.gif"/>
            </p>
            <p>
             As for family ties, I can easily love either.  While I dont mind the lone-wolf type, I like characters who are capable of strong emotional ties to others, whether they initially embrace those or not.  And those who do have strong family connections, well, often that makes for the start of an excellent series
             <img alt=":)" class="wp-smiley" src="http://bittenbybooks.com/wp-includes/images/smilies/icon_smile.gif"/>
            </p>
            <p>
             Congrats again on Unchainedare you doing anything special to celebrate or commemorate each new title?  (Dinner out? Framed coverflat? New bling? New body art?) (Do you have a keeper shelf at home for your own books? :))  And out of curiosity, who or whats on your keeper shelf?  Do you reread?
            </p>
            <p>
             Thanks for spending time with us today!
            </p>
            <p>
             Fedora C.
             <br/>
             - RSVPed
             <br/>
             - Tweeted:
             <a href="http://twitter.com/flchen1" rel="nofollow">
              http://twitter.com/flchen1
             </a>

             - commented at Bitten by Books Screen Bites
             <br/>
             - attended Erin Kellisons event
             <br/>
             - commented on Off the Fang
             <br/>
             - voted in the poll
            </p>

           <div class="author-comment">
            <cite class="fn">
             cories
            </cite>
            <div class="comment-meta commentmetadata">
             <a href="http://bittenbybooks.com/author-sharon-ashwood-release-party-and-contest-live-here/#comment-167498">
              July 8, 2010 at 4:23 pm
             </a>
            </div>
            <!-- .comment-meta .commentmetadata -->
           </div>
           <div class="clear">
           </div>
           <div class="comment-content">
            <p>
             My favorite vampire is still the classic Dracula.  He is the one on which all others are based.
            </p>
            <p>
             Although Dracula is not presented with a close family, he is part of a family of sorts: he has those women in Transylvania and then Renfield as his servant.  So, hes not a lone wolf.  Even lone wolves need to have some sort of family since otherwise there would be nobody for them to interact with (in such a way as to reveal more personality/character development).
            </p>
            <p>
             I RSVPd yesterday.
            </p>
            <p>
             Sheree T

             <br/>

            <p>
             Buffy is classic, one of the first that I came to know, so I like her. I liked Cat, from Jeaniene Frosts series and I like my vampire slayer thats in the book Im writing!
             <img alt=";)" class="wp-smiley" src="http://bittenbybooks.com/wp-includes/images/smilies/icon_wink.gif"/>
            </p>
            <p>
             Ooh vampire! Love Bones from Jeaniene Frosts series, loved Spike too! I liked Jeanne Steins Anna.
            </p>
            <p>
             For either question I really cant provide just one answer!
            </p>
            <p>
             I like both. I like the character with strong family ties, because I can relate to that. I am close to my immediate family at least and I like seeing that in my fictional characters. But the lone wolf type can be interesting too. They have reasons for not being attached to their families.
            </p>
            <p>
             What was your road to publication like? I keep asking this of many authors, but I like to know the different roads people take.
             <img alt=":)" class="wp-smiley" src="http://bittenbybooks.com/wp-includes/images/smilies/icon_smile.gif"/>
             Im an aspiring writer, so do you have any advice?
            </p>
            <p>
             I RSVP
             <br/>
             I posted on my blog:
             <a href="http://jessica-agreatread.blogspot.com" rel="nofollow">
              http://jessica-agreatread.blogspot.com
             </a>
             <br/>
             I was at the Chloe Neill event
             <br/>
             I voted
             <br/>
             I commented on the BBB Screen Bites
             <br/>
             I was at the Erin Kellison event

              <!-- .comment-meta .commentmetadata -->

             <div class="clear">
             </div>
             <div class="comment-content">
              <p>
               Hi, Jessica,
              </p>
              <p>
               I got a publishing contract through a contest sponsored by my local chapter of the Romance Writers of America. My advice is to join the RWA, because it gives the best concrete, practical advice of any organization Ive found. Also, try and find a good critique group, either in person or on line. Theyre not for everyone, but I have got a lot of value out of the experience and still belong to one. Its definitely worth trying out.
              </p>
             </div>
             <div class="reply">

               Hi Koren,
              </p>
              <p>
               Random plot bunnies are too valuable to let them escape.  I jot them down in an ideas file and let them stew until the time is right. I have both big and small goals, and I always reward myself. Its important to play fair with yourself, or you wont believe it when you make yourself promises!
              </p>

             <br/>
             My interest in your work and similar authors writing in the genre is professional. Im the entire staff of a small public library. Six months ago we split out paranormal romance (loosely defined)into a separate shelf location. Interest went through the roof, both from our patrons and via interlibrary loan. I even turned a retired logger on to it and hes read half the collection thus far. I couldnt be happier. as for the questions,
             <br/>
             Who is your favorite slayer character? Patricia Briggs Mercedes Thompson.
            </p>

              </p>

               I have a great critique group! There are about six of us.  I also have Beta readers  a few honest friends who read my work before it sees the light of day.
              </p>
              <p>
               Its hard to say how long it took to get published. I published the first book I got serious about preparing for publication, but Id written about five for fun before that.
              </p>
              <p>
               When I published my first book I bought myself a beautiful dark purple brocade jacket.

              <div class="comment-meta commentmetadata">

                July 9, 2010 at 12:05 am
               </a>
              </div>
              <!-- .comment-meta .commentmetadata -->
             </div>
             <div class="clear">
             </div>
             <div class="comment-content">
              <p>
               I really got the writing bug in high school.  I had a great English teacher who let me out of all my assignments if I wrote my first novel.  How great was that? So, I finished my first full-length book at age 16. I owe her a lot!
              </p>
              <p>
               Most of the books Ive written have a paranormal element. Its always been my reading choice, so it makes sense Id write the same way!
              </p>
              <p>
               Thanks so much for joining the chat!
              </p>
             </div>

             Sharon- This sounds like a series I could seriously get into! It is nice to see when an author is able to mix reality (a single working mother) with fantasy (vampires, ect.) To me it seems that just makes the story seem easier to grasp since you dont have to try to imagine a whole new world, your just adding more to what we have.
             <img alt=":)" class="wp-smiley" src="http://bittenbybooks.com/wp-includes/images/smilies/icon_smile.gif"/>
            </p>

             As far as a fav slayer- Raven Crosse from Kiss Me Deadly by Michele Hauf.
            </p>
            <p>
             Fav vampire- A cross between Eric Northman from Sookie Stackhouse series and all of the Brothers from Black Dagger Brotherhood by J.D. Ward.
            </p>
            <p>
             I preffer to see the family togetherness instead of a a lone wolf but its nice to see a lone wolf finally fit into a family later in a story!

             Who is your all-time favourite vampire?
             <br/>
             I would have to say that I love Christopher Pikes Sita from the Last Vampire series (or what theyre re-releasing as the Thirst series).  The way her lifestyle and feelings are described, I just feel that she is a true vampire.  When you read it, you can FEEL how long that shes lived in the infliction in her voice and by her attitudes towards others.
            </p>
            <p>
             Do you prefer characters who have strong family ties, or the
            </p>

            </p>

            </p>
